Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Marrying Sister of Wife Given Bā'in Divorce During 'Iddah
Ruling that marriage to sister of a woman given bā'in divorce is impermissible until her 'iddah ends

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the sister of a woman given bā'in divorce during her 'iddah, and explain the evidence and the dispute with the Shafi‘i school.

Core Idea
A woman in bā'in divorce remains a 'wife in some respects' during her 'iddah, making her sister forbidden.

A man divorces his wife with a bā'in (irrevocable) divorce. While she is still in her waiting period ('iddah), he wishes to marry her sister. Is this permissible? The Hanafi school answers with a firm 'no', based on the principle that the 'iddah retains some marital effects. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof from the Companions, and the contrasting view of Imam al-Shafi‘i.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the Hanafi position
Identify the precise question: may a man marry the sister of his former wife during the wife's 'iddah after a bā'in divorce? State the Hanafi ruling clearly.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
Locate the two athar (from ‘Ali and Ibn ‘Abbas) cited in the passage. Understand why they support the prohibition: they link the prohibition to the continuation of the 'iddah.
The athar explicitly forbid marrying a 'fifth' or the sister until the 'iddah expires.
3
Identify the Shafi‘i position and its proof
Understand the opposing view: Imam al-Shafi‘i permits the marriage immediately because bā'in divorce completely severs the marital bond. The 'iddah is merely a waiting period with no marital connection.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine how the Hanafi school rebuts the Shafi‘i argument: the 'iddah still carries legal effects (nafaqah, residence), so the woman is considered a wife 'min wajh' (from one aspect), which triggers the prohibition on marrying her sister.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: under the Hanafi school, the man must wait until the 'iddah ends; under the Shafi‘i school, he may marry immediately. This has real-world implications for timing of marriages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۷۴۶) (۲۱) اگر شوہر نے طلاق دی اپنی بیوی کو طلاق بائن تو نہیں جائز ہے اس کے لئے شادی کرے اس کی بہن سے یہاں تک کہ اس کی عدت گزر جائے۔ تشریح شوہر نے بیوی کو طلاق بائن دی، چاہے ایک طلاق دی یا تین طلاق دی۔ ابھی عدت نہیں گزری ہے کہ شوہر اس کی بہن سے شادی کرنا چاہتا ہے تو فرماتے ہیں کہ شادی نہیں کر سکتا جب تک کہ اس بیوی کی عدت ختم نہ ہو جائے اور مکمل طور پر شوہر سے علیحدہ نہ ہو جائے۔ (1) جب تک عدت باقی ہے اس وقت تک بیوی شوہر سے عدت کا نفقہ لے گی اور اس کی اجازت کے بغیر گھر سے باہر نہیں جائے گی۔ کیونکہ یہ شوہر کے لئے ہی عدت گزار رہی ہے تو گویا کہ یہ عورت عدت تک من وجہ بیوی ہے۔ اور جب یہ بیوی ہے تو اس کی بہن سے شادی نہیں کر سکتا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن علی قال لا يتزوج خامسة حتى تنقضي عدة التي طلق (الف)(مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ١١٦ في الرجل يكون تحته اربع نسوة فيطلق احداهن من كره ان يتزوج خامسة حتى تنقضى عدة التي طلق ج ثالث، ص ۵۱۷، نمبر ۱۶۷۳۹) (۳) عن عمر ابن شعيب قال طلق رجل امرأة ثم تزوج اختها قال ابن عباس لمروان : فرق بينها وبينه حتى تنقضى عدة التي طلق (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی هیبته ۱۶ افی الرجل يكون تحته الوليدة فيطلقها طلاقا بائنا فترجع الى سيدها فيطها الزوجھا ان پر ابھا ؟ ج ثالث ص ۵۱۶ نمبر ۱۶۷۳۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ چار بیویاں ہوں اور ایک کو طلاق بائن دی تو جب تک اس کی عدت نہ گزر جائے پانچویں سے شادی نہیں کر سکتا۔ اور اسی طرح اس کی بہن سے بھی شادی نہیں کر سکتا۔ فائندہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر طلاق بائن دی ہو یا طلاق مغلظہ دی ہو تو عدت کے اندر بھی اس کی بہن سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ یا چوتھی کو طلاق دی ہو تو عدت کے اندر ہی پانچویں سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ طلاق بائن اور طلاق مغلظہ میں عورت شوہر سے منقطع ہو جاتی ہے۔ چاہے عدت نہ گزری ہو اس لئے اس کی بہن سے شادی جا ئز ہے۔

حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت علی نے فرمایا پانچویں عورت سے شادی نہ کرے یہاں تک کہ اس کی عدت گزر جائے جس کو طلاق دی ہے ( ب ) حضرت عمر بن شعیب نے کہا کہ ایک آدمی نے طلاق دی پھر اس کی بہن سے شادی کی تو ابن عباس نے مروان سے کہا دونوں میں جدائیگی کر دو یہاں تک کہ جس کو طلاق دی ہے اس کی عدت گزر جائے۔
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling: it is not permissible for a man who has given his wife a bā'in (irrevocable) divorce to marry her sister until the divorced wife's 'iddah (waiting period) expires. The commentator explains that this applies whether the divorce was one or three. The rationale is that during the 'iddah, the wife is still considered a wife 'min wajh' (in some respects): she receives maintenance (nafaqah) and must stay in the husband's home without permission to leave. Therefore, she is effectively still connected to the husband, making her sister forbidden. The author then provides two athar (reports) as evidence: (1) ‘Ali’s statement: 'Do not marry a fifth [woman] until the 'iddah of the one you divorced expires.' (2) Ibn ‘Abbas’s instruction to Marwan regarding a man who divorced and then married the sister: 'Separate between them until the 'iddah of the divorced woman expires.' These show that the prohibition applies even when the husband has four wives and divorces one—he cannot marry a fifth during her 'iddah. The passage then notes that Imam al-Shafi‘i disagrees, holding that in bā'in or mughallazah (irrevocable or severe) divorce, the marriage is entirely severed, so the sister may be married immediately during the 'iddah. The Hanafi school relies on the athar and the legal principle that the 'iddah retains some marital effects.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (ṭalāq bā'in): Irrevocable divorce; the marriage is dissolved immediately, but the wife must observe an 'iddah.
عدت (‘iddah): The waiting period after divorce during which the woman cannot remarry. In this context, it is the period during which the sister of the divorced woman is forbidden to the husband.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Maintenance; the divorced wife is entitled to it during the 'iddah of a bā'in divorce according to Hanafis, indicating continued marital connection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it impermissible to marry the sister of a woman given bā'in divorce during her 'iddah?
A) Because the divorce is not yet effective until the 'iddah ends.
B) Because the ex-wife is still considered a wife in some respects (min wajh) during 'iddah.
C) Because marrying the sister would require the ex-wife's permission.
D) Because the sister of an ex-wife is always forbidden regardless of 'iddah.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a woman given bā'in divorce is still considered a wife 'min wajh' during her 'iddah, making her sister forbidden to the husband until the 'iddah ends.

Ruling on Mut'ah for Divorced Women and the Exception
States the ruling on mut'ah with an exception and proofs from Quran and Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific case where mut'ah becomes wajib in Hanafi fiqh and apply the Quranic proof (Surah al-Baqarah 2:236) to justify the ruling.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is mustahabb for all divorced women except one: the woman divorced before consummation with no specified dower — for her it is wajib.

The Hanafi school holds a nuanced position on the gift (mut'ah) given to divorced women. While generally recommended, one specific situation requires it as an obligation. In this lesson, we will examine that exception, its Quranic proof, and the reasoning behind the Hanafi distinction. This ruling demonstrates how an imperative in the Quran is interpreted to establish wujub in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and the exception
State the default ruling (mustahabb for every divorced woman) and pinpoint the one exception (the woman divorced before dukhul without a specified mahr).
The exception is introduced by 'illa' (except) in the text.
2
Locate the Quranic proof and its imperative form
Find Surah al-Baqarah 2:236 and note the imperative verb 'mattiu' (provide for them). This is the primary dalil.
The verse addresses the case where no dower was specified and no intercourse occurred.
3
Apply Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub
According to Hanafi principles, an imperative (amr) indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a qarinah (contextual evidence) to the contrary. Here, no qarinah weakens the imperative, so mut'ah is wajib.
Other schools may accept the imperative but interpret it as recommendatory due to other evidence.
4
Distinguish the exception with the hadith of Ibn Umar
The hadith confirms that a woman with a specified dower divorced before dukhul receives half the dower, so mut'ah is not needed. This reinforces that the Quranic imperative applies only when no dower is specified.
The hadith provides the line between the general rule and the exception.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on khalwat sahiha
The text digresses to a related issue: if the husband is sick or mutilated, valid seclusion (khalwat sahiha) does not occur according to the Sahibayn, affecting dower and mut'ah. This illustrates the complexity of applying conditions.
This step is optional but shows the depth of Hanafi legal reasoning.

بیمار کو سپرد کرنے سے خلوت صحیحہ نہیں ہوتی ہے تو محبوب الذکر تو اس سے زیادہ بیمار کے درجے میں ہے۔اس لئے اس کو سپر د کر نے سے بھی خلوت صحیحہ نہیں ہوگی اور پورا مہر لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ ۱۷۹۳ (۶۸) مستحب ہے نہ کچھ ملنا چاہئے ۔ اس لئے اس کے لئے متعہ دینا واجب کریں گے (۲) ایسی عورت کو متعہ دینے کے لئے آیت میں امر کا صیغہ استعمال کیا ہے لا جناح عليكم ان طلقتم النساء مالم تمسوهن او تفرضوا لهن فريضة ومتعوهن على الموسع قدره وعلى المقتر قدره متاعا بالمعروف (الف) (آیت ۲۳۶ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں فرمایا جس کے لئے مہر متعین نہ کیا ہو اور اس سے خلوت صحیحہ بھی نہ کیا ہو اس کوضرور متعہ دو اپنی حیثیت کے مطابق ۔ اس کی تغیر عبداللہ بن عباس سے (سن للبیہقی ، باب التفویض ج سابع نہ ہواس اس بن ن ص ۲۴۴) پر گزر چکی ہے۔ ائندہ اگر مہر متعین ہو اور محبت سے پہلے طلاق ہوئی ہو تو اس کو آدھا مہر ملے گا ۔ اور مال سپرد کئے بغیر آدھا مہر ملا ہے اس لئے اس کو متعہ دینا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ (۱) عن ابن عمر انه كان يقول لكل مطلقة متعة الا التي تطلق وقد فرض لها الصداق ولم تمس فحسبها نصف ما فرض لها (ب) (سن للمبنى ، باب المحتہ ج سادس بس ۲۱۹، نمبر ۱۴۴۹) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ جس کا مہر متعین ہوا اور صحبت سے پہلے طلاق دیدے تو اس کو آدھا مہر ملے گا۔ اس لئے اس کے لئے متعہ ضروری نہیں ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) تم پر کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے اگر تم عورت کو طلاق دو اور اس کو چھوڑ نہیں اور اس کے لئے مہر متعین نہ کرو۔ اور ان کو متعہ دو مالدار کو وسعت کے مطابق اور تنگدست کو اس کی وسعت کے مطابق فائدہ اٹھانے دیتا ہے معروف کے ساتھ (ب) حضرت ابن عمر فرماتے ہیں کہ ہر مطلقہ کے لئے متعہ ہے مگر جس کو طلاق دے اور اس کے لئے مہر متعین کیا ہو اور عورت کو ہاتھ نہ لگایا تو اس کو کافی ہے اس کا آدھا جتنا اس کے لئے متعین کیا ہے۔
Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) (68) Mut'ah is recommended for every divorced woman except one: she who was divorced before consummation and for whom no dower was specified. 19 (29) And if a man marries [a woman] on [the condition of] a mutilated male, full dower is obligatory. The two companions say that consigning a sick person does not constitute valid seclusion, so the beloved male is even more in the position of a sick person. Therefore, consigning him also does not constitute valid seclusion, and full dower is not obligatory. 1793 (68) Mut'ah is recommended for every divorced woman except one: she who was divorced before intercourse and for whom no dower was specified. It is recommended to give mut'ah cloth to all divorced women, but for one woman it is obligatory to give cloth. She is the one for whom no dower was specified and who was divorced before valid seclusion; she will not receive dower. Because the dower was not specified; if intercourse had occurred, she would have received dower of the like, and before intercourse half of the dower of the like is not [due], so she must receive something. Therefore, we deem it obligatory to give her mut'ah. To give mut'ah to such a woman, the imperative form is used in the verse: 'There is no sin upon you if you divorce women when you have not touched them nor specified for them an obligation, but provide for them – for the wealthy according to his means and for the poor according to his means – a provision in the proper manner' (a) (Surah al-Baqarah 2:236). In this verse, it is said: for her whose dower was not specified and with whom valid seclusion did not occur, you must give mut'ah according to your capacity. Its interpretation from Abdullah ibn Abbas (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Tafwid, volume 7, page 244) has passed. Thereafter, if the dower is specified and divorce occurred before intercourse, she receives half the dower. And without handing over property, half the dower is received, so giving her mut'ah is not necessary. (1) From Ibn Umar that he used to say: Every divorced woman gets mut'ah except the one who is divorced while her dower was specified and she was not touched; then half of what was specified suffices her (b) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Mut'ah, volume 6, page 219, number 1449). From this it is known that she whose dower was specified and she was divorced before intercourse will receive half the dower. Therefore, mut'ah is not necessary for her. Footnote: (a) 'There is no sin upon you if you divorce women when you have not touched them nor specified for them an obligation, but provide for them – for the wealthy according to his means and for the poor according to his means – a provision in the proper manner.' (b) Ibn Umar says that every divorced woman gets mut'ah except the one who is divorced while her dower was specified and the woman was not touched; then half of what was specified suffices her.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the commentary of Al-Hidayah. It begins by stating the ruling on mut'ah (a gift given to a divorced woman). According to Abu Hanifa, giving mut'ah is recommended (mustahabb) for every divorced woman, except for one specific case. The exception is a woman who was divorced before consummation (dukhul) and for whom no dower (mahr) was specified at the time of marriage. For such a woman, mut'ah becomes obligatory (wajib). The passage then digresses into a related but distinct issue: if a man marries a woman on the condition that he will marry her to a male with a severed limb (or something similar), full dower is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa, but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that such a condition does not constitute valid seclusion (khalwat sahiha) because the husband is like a sick person, so the dower is not fully obligatory. The text then returns to explain the mut'ah ruling in detail: for the woman divorced before consummation without specified dower, she receives nothing from the marriage contract because no dower was set and no seclusion occurred, so she must be compensated with mut'ah. The Quranic proof is Surah al-Baqarah 2:236, which uses an imperative form (muttu) indicating obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi principles. The hadith from Ibn Umar confirms that a woman with a specified dower who is divorced before intercourse only receives half the dower, and thus no mut'ah. The passage also references the interpretation of Ibn Abbas. The footnote provides the full text of the verse and the hadith.

Key Terms
المتعة (al-mut'ah): A gift given to a divorced woman as compensation, usually clothing or something appropriate to the husband's means.
الخلوت الصحيحة (al-khalwat al-sahiha): Valid seclusion between husband and wife that is legally considered like actual intercourse for certain rules, such as giving half the dower upon divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, for which divorced woman is giving mut'ah obligatory?
A) A woman divorced after consummation with a specified dower
B) A woman divorced before consummation without a specified dower
C) A woman divorced before consummation with a specified dower
D) A woman divorced after consummation without a specified dower

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, mut'ah is wajib only for the woman divorced before consummation without a specified dower, supported by the imperative in Quran 2:236.

Marrying a Fifth Wife During Iddah: Hanafi Ruling and Proof
State ruling and provide athar-based proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a fifth wife while a divorced wife is in iddah and explain the proof from the athar of Ali and Amr ibn Shu'ayb.

Core Idea
A divorced wife in iddah still counts toward the limit of four, making a fifth marriage haram until iddah ends.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the intersection of polygamy and divorce. When a man has four wives and divorces one with a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce, the question arises: can he immediately marry another woman? The Hanafi position, grounded in the rulings of the Companions, is that he must wait until the divorced wife's iddah expires. The source passage provides both the ruling and its evidentiary basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is marrying a fifth woman when one of the four wives has been divorced with a ba'in divorce and is still in iddah. The ruling is haram (prohibited). Understood?
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two athar (reports from Companions and Successors) from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah. The first is directly from Ali ibn Abi Talib stating 'لا يتزوج خامسة حتى تنقضى عدة التي طلق'. The second from Amr ibn Shu'ayb deals with a related case (marrying the sister during iddah) reinforcing the principle.
The athar are of zanni thubut (probable transmission) but are accepted as evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit command 'لا يتزوج خامسة' (he shall not marry a fifth) indicates prohibition. The condition 'حتى تنقضى عدة التي طلق' (until the iddah of the one he divorced ends) establishes that the divorced woman still counts as a wife for the purpose of the limit of four. Her iddah maintains a marital link (min wajh).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi position is that the iddah preserves the marital count. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may argue that a ba'in divorce severs the marriage completely, so iddah does not affect the limit. But Hanafis rely on the athar and the rationale that iddah is for the protection of lineage and still connects the spouses in some respects.
The practical consequence (thamar al-khilaf): in the Hanafi school, the husband cannot marry a fifth during iddah; in other schools he may be permitted immediately.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi school adopts the position based on the explicit athar and the principle that during iddah the woman is still considered a wife 'min wajh' (in some respects). This is the mufta bihi (operative position) in the school.

احدى الاربع طلاقا بائنا لم يجز له ان يتزوج رابعة حتى تنقضي عدتها. پس اگر آزاد نے ایک کو طلاق بائنہ دی تو اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ چوتھی سے شادی کرے یہاں تک کہ اس کی عدت گزر جائے آزاد آدمی کے پاس چار بیویاں تھیں ۔ ان میں سے ایک طلاق کو بائنہ دی تو جب تک اس کی عدت نہ گزرے اور شوہر سے مکمل طور پر کے پاس چار ان میں سے ایک طلاق باندی تو نہ طور پر جدائیگی نہ ہو اس وقت تک پانچویں سے شادی نہیں کر سکتا۔ جب تک طلاق شدہ عورت کی عدت نہ گزر جائے اس وقت تک وہ من وجہ شوہر کی بیوی ہے۔ اور جب چار بیوی موجود ہیں تو پانچویں سے شادی نہیں کر سکتا اثر میں ہے عن علی قال لا يتزوج خامسة حتى تنقضى عدة التي طلق (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة افی الرجل یکون تحته اربع نسوة فيطلق احداهن ج ثالث ص ۵۵۷، نمبر ۱۶۷۳۹) دوسرے اثر میں ہے عن عمر بن شعیب قال طلق رجل امرأة ثم تزوج اختها في عدتها قال نكاحها حرام ويفرق بينها و بينه حتى تنقضى عدة التي طلق (مصنف ابن ابی هیتة ۱۶ افی الرجل يكون تحته الوليدة فيطلقها طلاقا با من فترجع الى سيدها فيطاً ها اكثر وجها ان يراجعھاج ثالث ص ۵۱۶، نمبر ۱۶۷۳۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جب تک عدت نہ گزر جائے پانچویں سے شادی نہیں کر سکتا۔
One of the four (wives) with a definitive divorce (ba'in), it is not permissible for him to marry a fourth (i.e., a fifth) until her iddah expires. Then if a free man gave one a ba'in divorce, it is not permissible for him to marry a fourth until her iddah passes. A free man had four wives. He gave one a ba'in divorce; until her iddah does not pass and she is completely separated from the husband, he cannot marry a fifth. As long as the divorced woman's iddah has not passed, she is, in some respects, the wife of the husband. And when there are four wives present, he cannot marry a fifth. There is an athar from Ali: he said, 'He should not marry a fifth until the iddah of the one he divorced expires.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) Another athar from Amr ibn Shu'ayb: he said, 'A man divorced a woman, then married her sister during her iddah; he said, her marriage is unlawful, and a separation is made between them until the iddah of the one he divorced expires.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) From this athar it is understood that as long as the iddah does not expire, he cannot marry a fifth.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding a man who has four wives and divorces one of them with a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce. The ruling states that he cannot marry another woman (a fifth) until the iddah of the divorced wife expires. The reason, as explained in the Urdu commentary, is that during the iddah, the divorced woman is still considered a wife in some respects (min wajh), so he still technically has four wives. The proof is provided through athar (reports from Companions and Successors). The first athar is from Ali ibn Abi Talib, explicitly stating that one should not marry a fifth until the iddah ends. The second athar from Amr ibn Shu'ayb deals with a related scenario: if a man divorces one woman and then marries her sister during the iddah of the first, that marriage is unlawful and must be annulled, emphasizing the ongoing marital connection during iddah.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that severs the marriage immediately, but the wife must observe iddah.
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman observes after divorce or death of husband before she can remarry.
أثر (athar): A report from a Companion or Successor, as opposed to a hadith from the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man has four wives. He divorces one with a ba'in divorce. The divorced wife's iddah is 90 days. After 30 days, can he marry another woman according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because the divorce is ba'in and her marriage is over.
B) No, because he must wait until her iddah expires.
C) Yes, if he marries in a different city.
D) No, because he must wait exactly 90 days from the divorce.

Key Takeaway
A ba'in divorcée in iddah counts as one of the four wives, prohibiting a fifth marriage until her iddah ends.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner
6 min
Types of Divorce: Ahsan, Sunnah, and Bid'ah
Defining the three categories of divorce based on timing and number of pronouncements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for each type of talaq (ahsan, sunnah, bid'ah) and distinguish them based on timing and number of pronouncements.

Core Idea
A single divorce in a pure state without intercourse is the best; three separate pronouncements over three pure periods is sunnah; any other method is bid'ah.

Divorce, though the most detestable of permissible acts, is sometimes necessary. The Hanafi school classifies the method of pronouncing divorce into three categories: ahsan (best), sunnah (following the prophetic practice), and bid'ah (innovation). Understanding these categories is essential for anyone who must initiate or advise on divorce, as they determine both religious merit and legal validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of divorce
From the passage, list the three categories: ahsan al-talaq (best divorce), talaq al-sunnah (sunnah divorce), and talaq al-bid'ah (innovation divorce). Note that the passage focuses on defining the first two and contrasts them with bid'ah.
The Urdu commentary clarifies that the best method (ahsan) is also sometimes called sunnah divorce, but the author distinguishes them.
2
Analyze the conditions for ahsan talaq
Identify the three conditions: (1) one pronouncement (taliqa wahida), (2) during a single period of purity (tuhr) in which no intercourse occurred, and (3) then letting the 'iddah expire without further action. Understand that this method allows reconciliation during the 'iddah.
3
Analyze the conditions for sunnah talaq
For a consummated wife (madkhul biha), sunnah divorce requires three pronouncements over three separate tuhr periods. Each pronouncement is given in a distinct period of purity. This method spaces the divorces and leaves room for retraction.
The text implies that this method is also recommended but not as preferred as ahsan.
4
Understand bid'ah talaq
Bid'ah divorce violates the sunnah – for example, pronouncing three divorces at once or divorcing during menstruation. Although sinful (haram), it is still legally effective; the divorce takes effect even though the method is prohibited.
This point is not detailed in the passage but is standard Hanafi fiqh.
5
Note the terminological nuance
The passage indicates that sometimes ahsan talaq is also called sunnah talaq. However, the author distinguishes them: ahsan is a single divorce with waiting, while sunnah is three divorces over three periods. Both are considered sunnah, but ahsan is better.
Be aware of this ambiguity in later texts.

Book of Divorce. [1885] (1) Divorce is of three types: the best divorce (ahsan al-talaq), the sunnah divorce (talaq al-sunnah), and the innovation divorce (talaq al-bid'ah). [16] (2) The best divorce is that a man divorces his wife with one pronouncement (taliqa wahida) during a single period of purity (tuhr) in which he has not had intercourse with her, and then he leaves her until her 'iddah expires. (3) And the sunnah divorce is that he divorces a woman who has been consummated... [Urdu continuation:] Divorce is the separation of a woman from marriage. Its proof is from this verse: 'Divorce is twice; then retention with honor or release with kindness' (a) (Verse 229 of Surah al-Baqarah). 'O Prophet! When you divorce women, divorce them for their 'iddah and count the 'iddah' (b) (Verse 1 of Surah al-Talaq). And in hadith: 'Ibn Umar narrated that the Prophet said: The most detestable of permissible things to Allah is divorce' (c) (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Dislike of Divorce, p. 303, no. 2178). From these verses and hadith, the permissibility of divorce is proven. [1885] (1) Divorce is of three types: ahsan, sunnah, and bid'ah. The three methods of divorce are described below. [1886] (2) Ahsan divorce is that a man gives his wife one divorce in a state of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her, then leaves her until her 'iddah expires. Divorce should not be given, but if compelled to give it, the best method is as described. It is called ahsan because within the 'iddah he can return to her if he wishes. (2) An athar: 'Abdullah said: Whoever wants the divorce that is truly divorce, let him give one divorce and then leave her until she completes three menstrual periods.' (d) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Section on What is Recommended of Sunnah Divorce and How It Is, vol. 4, p. 57, no. 7733; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter on the Manner of Divorce: It is the Divorce of 'Iddah and Its Sunnah, vol. 6, p. 301, no. 10920). From this athar it is understood that one should divorce in a state of purity without intercourse, then leave the woman until the 'iddah expires. This is ahsan talaq. Sometimes it is also called sunnah talaq. [1887] (3) And sunnah divorce is that he gives three divorces to a consummated wife over three periods of purity. Footnotes: (a) Divorce is twice; then either retain with honor or release with kindness. (b) O Prophet! When you divorce women, divorce them for their 'iddah and count the 'iddah. (c) The Prophet said: The most detestable of permissible things to Allah is divorce. (d) Whoever wants the proper divorce should give one divorce and then leave her until three menstruations.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Divorce defines the three categories of talaq. The best (ahsan) is a single divorce during a tuhr (non-menstrual period) without intercourse, followed by letting the 'iddah expire. This allows for possible reconciliation. The sunnah method is to give one divorce in each of three successive tuhr periods. The bid'ah method (mentioned but not detailed here) is contrary to the sunnah. The text also provides Quranic and hadith proofs for the legitimacy of divorce. Note that the ahsan method is often called 'sunnah talaq' by some, but the author distinguishes between ahsan and sunnah. The athar from Abdullah (likely Ibn Mas'ud) supports the single pronouncement method. The passage is foundational for understanding the procedural rules of divorce in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
احسن طلاق (ahsan al-talaq): The best divorce: one pronouncement during a non-menstruous period without intercourse, followed by waiting for the 'iddah to expire.
طلاق السنّة (talaq al-sunnah): Sunnah divorce: for a consummated wife, to pronounce one divorce in each of three tuhr periods.
طلاق البدعة (talaq al-bid'ah): Innovation divorce: any divorce that violates the sunnah, such as pronouncing three divorces in one sitting or divorcing during menstruation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The method of divorce matters: the best (ahsan) uses one pronouncement with waiting; the sunnah uses three spaced over three pure periods; departure from these is bid'ah (sinful but valid).

Definition of Talaq and Its Three Types
Defines talaq, cites scriptural evidence, and categorizes it into three types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define talaq, identify its three types, and state its ruling (permissible but detestable) with evidence from Quran and Hadith.

Core Idea
Talaq is the most detestable permissible act — it is lawful but strongly disliked.

This lesson opens the Book of Talaq by defining divorce as the dissolution of the marriage contract. The author establishes its permissibility from clear Quranic verses and a well-known hadith, while also noting its severe dislike in the sight of Allah. He then outlines the three categories of talaq — Ahsan, Sunnah, and Bid'a — which will be explored in detail subsequently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Locate the term 'talaq' and recognize that the passage is defining this legal act. Note its Urdu definition: separating a wife from marriage.
Focus on the definition: dissolution of marriage contract.
2
Extract the legal definition
The passage states 'عورت کو نکاح سے الگ کرنے کو طلاق کہتے ہیں' — divorce is called separating a wife from marriage. Understand that this is the legal meaning.
Compare with other possible definitions (linguistic vs. legal).
3
Identify the scriptural proofs
Find the Quranic verses (2:229, 65:1) and the hadith (Ibn Umar) that establish the permissibility of talaq. Note that the Quran commands either retention with honor or release with kindness, and the hadith labels it the most detestable of permissible things.
The proofs show talaq is permitted but disliked.
4
Determine the ruling
From the proofs, conclude that talaq is legally permissible (halal) but carries a strong detestation (makruh tanzih). It is not haram nor obligatory.
The hadith explicitly calls it 'halal' yet detestable.
5
Enumerate the three types
The passage lists three types: Ahsan (best), Sunnah (following prophetic practice), and Bid'a (innovated). Recognize that these are based on the timing and manner of pronouncement.
Further details about each type will follow in subsequent lessons.

كتاب الطلاق
الطلاق على ثلثة اوجه احسن الطلاق وطلاق السنة وطلاق البدعة
عورت کو نکاح سے الگ کرنے کو طلاق کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا ثبوت اس آیت سے ہے۔ الطلاق مرتان فامساک بمعروف او تسريح باحسان (الف) ( آیت ۲۲۹ سورة البقرة (۲) یا ايها النبى اذا طلقتم النساء فطلقوهن لعدتهن واحصوا العدة (ب) (آیت اسورۃ الطلاق (۶۵) اور حدیث میں ہے (۲) عن ابن عمر عن النبي الله قال ابغض الحلال الى الله عز وجل الطلاق (ج) ( ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی کراہیۃ الطلاق ص ۳۰۳ نمبر ۲۱۷۸) ان آیتوں اور حدیث سے طلاق دینے کا ثبوت ہوا۔ [۱۸۸۵) (۱) طلاق کی تین قسمیں ہیں۔ احسن طلاق ، طلاق سنت اور طلاق بدعت۔
طلاق دینے کے تین طریقے ہیں ان کی تفصیل آگے آ رہی ہے۔
Book of Divorce. Divorce is of three types: the best divorce, the Sunna divorce, and the innovated divorce. Divorce is called separating a wife from marriage. Its proof is from this verse: 'Divorce is twice, then retention with honor or release with goodness' (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:229) (a) 'O Prophet, when you divorce women, divorce them for their waiting period and count the waiting period' (Surah al-Talaq, 65:1) (b). And in hadith: 'From Ibn Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: The most detestable of permissible things to Allah Almighty is divorce' (c) (Abu Dawud, chapter on dislike of divorce, p. 303 no. 2178). From these verses and hadith, the permission of giving divorce is established. [1885] (1) Divorce has three types: Ahsan divorce, Sunna divorce, and Bid'a divorce. There are three methods of giving divorce; their details are coming ahead.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Talaq. The author first defines talaq in Urdu as the act of separating a wife from the marriage contract. He then provides scriptural evidence: Quran 2:229 establishes the basic permissibility of divorce with the instruction to either retain with honor or release with kindness; Quran 65:1 commands that divorce be given at the start of the waiting period (i.e., in a state of purity without intercourse). The hadith from Ibn Umar declares divorce to be the most detestable lawful act to Allah, indicating its strong dislike. Based on these, the ruling that talaq is permissible (ja'iz) but makruh (disliked) is established. The passage then announces that talaq has three forms: Ahsan (best), Sunnah (following prophetic practice), and Bid'a (innovative). This sets the stage for the detailed discussion that follows. In the Hanafi school, all three types are effective in dissolving the marriage, but the first two are in accordance with the Sunnah and preferred, while the third is sinful yet valid.

Key Terms
الطلاق (al-talaq): Legally, it is the dissolution of the marriage contract by the husband's pronouncement.
احسن الطلاق (ahsan al-talaq): The best form of divorce, where the husband pronounces one talaq during a period of purity (tuhr) without intercourse, then leaves her to complete the waiting period.
طلاق السنة (talaq al-sunnah): The Sunna divorce, where the husband pronounces one talaq during a period of purity, or three talaqs over three months (one per month).
طلاق البدعة (talaq al-bid'a): The innovated divorce, which violates the Sunnah, e.g., pronouncing three divorces at once or divorcing during menstruation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is haram
B) It is the most detestable of permissible things to Allah
C) It is obligatory
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
Talaq is legally permissible (mubah) but is the most detestable of permissible acts to Allah (makruh tanzih), making it a permitted yet highly discouraged action.

Talaq — Divorce

Ahsan Talaq: The Best Form of Divorce
Defines ahsan talaq with conditions and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of ahsan talaq and apply them to identify whether a divorce follows the recommended method.

Core Idea
Ahsan talaq: one divorce in a pure state without intercourse, then wait for 'idda.

Divorce is generally disliked, but when necessary, the Hanafi school prescribes a specific method that offers the possibility of reconciliation. This passage defines the 'best divorce' (ahsan talaq) and provides its conditions, along with a companion's statement (athar) supporting the practice. Understanding this method helps you distinguish between the sunna (praiseworthy) and bid‘i (innovative) forms of divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage describes 'ahsan talaq' and implicitly gives it the ruling of sunnah muakkadah (recommended) when divorce is unavoidable.
2
List the conditions
Extract the three key conditions: (1) the divorce is pronounced during a state of purity (tuhr), (2) no intercourse occurred during that purity, (3) only one divorce (talaq wahid) is given. After that, the husband leaves her until the 'idda (waiting period) ends.
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites an athar from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (رضی اللہ عنہ) that commands a single pronouncement and waiting for three menstruations. Identify the type of dalil (qawl sahabi) and its chain.
4
Derive the ruling from the dalil
The imperative 'falyutalliqha' indicates a recommended method; the context 'the divorce that is the divorce' shows it is the preferred way.
5
Note the practical benefit
Ahsan talaq allows the husband to revoke the divorce during the 'idda, preserving the possibility of reconciliation. This is why it is called 'best'.

[۱۸۸۶) (۲) احسن طلاق یہ ہے کہ آدمی اپنی بیوی کو ایک طلاق دے ایسے طہر میں کہ جس میں اس سے وطی نہ کی ہو۔ پھر اس کو چھوڑ دے یہاں تک کہ اس کی عدت گزر جائے۔ یوں تو طلاق نہیں دینی چاہئے لیکن اگر مجبوری میں دینی ہی پڑے تو اس کا احسن طریقہ یہ ہے کہ جس طہر میں صحبت نہ کی ہو اس طہر میں ایک طلاق دے کر چھوڑ دے۔ یہاں تک کہ عدت گزر کر خود بائنہ ہو جائے۔ احسن اس لئے کہا کہ عدت کے اندر رجوع کرنا چاہے تو کر سکتا ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے ۔ عن عبد الله قال من اراد الطلاق الذي هو الطلاق فليطلقها تطليقة ثم يدعها حتى تحيض ثلاث حيض ( د ) ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ٢ ما يستحب من طلاق السنة وكيف هو؟ ج رابع ص ۵۷، نمبر ۷۷۳۳ار مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب وجہ الطلاق و هو طلاق العدة و سنتهج سادس ص ۳۰۱ نمبر ۱۰۹۲۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایسے طہر میں طلاق دے جس میں جماع نہ کیا ہو۔ پھر عورت کو چھوڑ دے یہاں تک کہ عدت گزر جائے یہ احسن طلاق ہے۔ اور بعض مرتبہ اس کو طلاق سنت بھی کہتے ہیں۔
[1886] (2) The best divorce (ahsan talaq) is that a man gives his wife a single divorce in a state of purity (tuhr) in which he has not had intercourse with her, then leaves her until her waiting period expires. Divorce should not be given, but if compelled, the best method is to give a single divorce in a pure state without intercourse, then leave her until the waiting period ends and she becomes irrevocably separated. It is called 'best' because he can return to her during the waiting period if he wishes. (2) In the athar: 'From Abdullah, he said: Whoever intends the divorce that is the divorce, let him divorce her once, then leave her until she experiences three menstruations.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, etc.) From this athar, it is learned that divorce should be given in a pure state without intercourse, then leave her until the waiting period expires. This is the best divorce, and sometimes it is also called sunna divorce.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage describes the first and best type of talaq: Ahsan talaq. The conditions are: (1) the wife must have been in a state of purity (tuhr) at the time of pronouncement, (2) the husband must not have had intercourse during that purity, (3) only one pronouncement (talaq wahida) is given, and (4) the husband then refrains from sexual relations until the wife's 'idda (waiting period) expires, after which the divorce becomes irrevocable (ba'in). The advantage of this method is that the husband can revoke (رجوع) the divorce during the 'idda. The text then provides a supporting athar (statement of a Companion) from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (رضي الله عنه) emphasizing a single pronouncement and waiting for three menstrual cycles. This aligns with the Hanafi preference for the best method. Note that the text mentions 'sometimes it is called sunna talaq' because it follows the sunna, but the following lesson distinguishes sunna talaq as a different category.

Key Terms
احسن الطلاق (ahsan al-talaq): The best form of divorce: a single pronouncement in a state of purity without intercourse, followed by leaving the wife until her 'idda expires.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for ahsan talaq regarding intercourse?
A) The husband must have intercourse in that purity
B) The husband must not have intercourse in that purity
C) Intercourse is irrelevant
D) The wife must be menstruating

Key Takeaway
Ahsan talaq is a single divorce pronounced during a non-menstrual purity without prior intercourse, followed by waiting for the 'idda to expire, and this method is the recommended practice in the Hanafi school.

Talaq — Divorce

Sunna Talaq: The Prophetic Method of Divorce
Defines sunna talaq with conditions and provides hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of sunna talaq and apply the Hanafi ruling to distinguish between consummated and non-consummated wives.

Core Idea
Sunna divorce requires three pronouncements in three pure periods without intercourse – only applies to consummated wives.

In the Hanafi school, divorce can be carried out in one of two recommended ways: aḥsan (best) and sunna (prophetic). This lesson focuses on sunna talaq, the method taught by the Prophet ﷺ for divorcing a wife with whom marriage has been consummated. The key conditions involve timing and purity, as established by authentic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage defines ṭalāq al-sunna as a recommended method of divorce. Identify that it applies only to a madkhūl bihā wife and that it is sunnah (recommended).
The ruling level is sunnah, not wājib.
2
Distinguish between consummated and non-consummated wives
The text explicitly restricts sunna talaq to a wife with whom intercourse has occurred. For a non-consummated wife, even a single divorce causes immediate irrevocable separation, so the concept of ‘three divorces in three tuhrs’ does not apply.
This distinction is crucial for proper application.
3
Understand the required conditions
The divorce must be pronounced in a state of purity (ṭuhr), and no sexual intercourse must have occurred in that purity. The phrase ‘ثلاثا في ثلاثة أطهار’ indicates one divorce per pure period.
The absence of intercourse is derived from the hadith.
4
Analyze the hadith proofs
Two hadith are cited. The first (from Ibn Mas‘ūd) describes the method: one pronouncement in purity without intercourse, then wait for menstruation and purity, then another. The second (from Ibn ‘Umar) provides the ruling that divorcing during menstruation is forbidden and must be revoked, and that the correct time is purity without intercourse.
Notice the Prophet’s command ‘طلِّق قبل أن يمس’ (divorce before touching).
5
Note the superiority of aḥsan
The text mentions that sunna talaq is of a lower degree than aḥsan because it results in three divorces, requiring ḥalāla for remarriage. Understand that while valid, aḥsan (one divorce and waiting for the ‘idda) is more recommended.
This preference is based on the desire to avoid unnecessary difficulty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطلاق السنة ان تطلق المدخول بها ثلاثا في ثلاثة اطهار
[۱۸۸۷] (۳) اور طلاق سنت یہ ہے کہ طلاق دے مدخول بہا کو تین ! تین طہروں میں۔
حاشیہ : (الف) طلاق دو مرتبہ ہے۔ پھر اچھے انداز میں روک لیتا ہے یا احسان کے ساتھ چھوڑ دیتا ہے (ب) اے نبی اگر بیویوں کو طلاق دو تو عدت گزارنے کے مناسب طلاق دیں اور عدت کو گئیں (ج) آپ نے فرمایا اللہ تعالی و حلال میں سے مبغوض چیز طلاق ہے (د) جو مناسب طلاق دینا چاہے تو وہ ایک طلاق دیدے ۔ پھر اس کو تین حیض تک چھوڑ دے۔
بها ثلاثا في ثلاثة اطهار
جس عورت سے صحبت نہیں کی ہے اس کو ایک طلاق بھی دے گا تو وہ فورا بائنہ ہوکر جدا ہو جائے گی۔ اور دوسری اور تیسری طلاق دینے کا محل باقی نہیں رہتی۔ اور اس پر عدت نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے جس عورت سے صحبت نہ کی ہو اس کو تین مجلس میں تین طلاق نہیں دے سکتا۔ تین مجلس میں تین طلاقیں تو صحبت شدہ عورت کو دے سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کے لئے سنت یہ ہے کہ تین طہروں میں تین طلاقیں دے۔ یہ سنت طریقہ ہے لیکن چونکہ عورت کو تین طہروں میں تین طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی اور حلالہ کرانے کی ضرورت پڑے گی اس لئے یہ پہلی والی سے کم درجہ ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد اللـه انـه قـال طلاق السنة تطليقة وهي طاهر في غير جماع فاذا حاضت وظهرت طلقها اخرى فاذا حاضت وطهرت طلقها اخرى ثم تعتد بعد ذلك بحيضة (الف) (نسائی شریف، باب طلاق النبی ص ۴۷۵ نمبر ۳۴۲۳ ردار قطنی، کتاب الطلاق ج رابع ص نمبر ۳۸۴۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہر طہر میں ایک طلاق دے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ عبد اللہ بن عمر نے اپنی بیوی کو حیض کی حالت میں طلاق دی تو آپ نے رجعت کرنے کا حکم دیا پھر فرمایا کہ جب طہر آجائے تو اس میں چاہے تو طلاق دے اور چاہے تو بیوی رکھ لے۔ حدیث یہ ہے عن عبد الله بن عمر انه طلق امرأته وهي حائض على عهد رسول الله فسأل عمر بن الخطاب رسول الله الا الله عن ذلك فقال رسول الله له مره فليراجعها ثم ليمسكها صلى الله عليه وسلم حتى تطـهـر ثـم تـحـيـض ثم تطهر ثم ان شاء امسك بعد وان شاء طلق قبل ان يمس فتلك العدة التي امر الله ان يطلق لها النساء (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب وقول الله تعالی یا لکھا النبی از اطلقتم النساء فطلقوهن لعد تھن واحسوا العدة ( آيت اسورۃ الطلاق ۶۵ ، ص ۷۹۱ نمبر (۵۲۵) مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم طلاق الحائض بغیر رضا حاص ۴۷۶ نمبر ۱ ۱۴۷ ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی طلاق النبی ص ۳۰۳ نمبر ۲۱۷۹) اس آیت اور حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایسے طہر میں طلاق دے جس میں جماع نہ کیا ہو۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ حیض کی حالت میں طلاق دینا مبغوض ہے۔
And the Sunna divorce is that he divorces a consummated wife three times in three pure periods. [1887] (3) And Sunna divorce is that he gives divorce to a consummated wife three times in three tuhrs. Footnote: (a) Divorce is twice; then retain with honor or release with goodness. (b) O Prophet, when you divorce women, divorce them for their waiting period and count the waiting period. (c) The Prophet said: The most detestable of permissible things to Allah is divorce. (d) Whoever wants to give a proper divorce, let him divorce her once, then leave her until three menstruations. In three tuhrs. For a woman with whom intercourse has not occurred, if he gives even one divorce, she becomes immediately irrevocably separated, and there is no place for a second or third divorce, and she has no waiting period. Therefore, for a non-consummated wife, he cannot give three divorces in three assemblies. He can only give three divorces in three assemblies to a consummated wife. So for a consummated wife, the sunna method is to give three divorces in three tuhrs. This is the sunna method, but since the woman will receive three divorces in three tuhrs and will need halala, it is of a lower degree than the first (ahsan). (2) In hadith: 'Abdullah said: The sunna divorce is a single pronouncement while she is pure without intercourse; when she menstruates and becomes pure, divorce her again; when she menstruates and becomes pure, divorce her again; then she observes 'idda with one menstruation after that.' (Nasa'i, etc.) This hadith instructs to give one divorce each tuhr. (2) Another hadith: 'Abdullah ibn Umar divorced his wife while she was menstruating during the time of the Prophet, so Umar asked the Prophet about that, and he said: Command him to take her back, then keep her until she becomes pure, then menstruates, then becomes pure; then if he wishes, he may keep her, and if he wishes, he may divorce her before touching her. That is the waiting period which Allah has commanded to divorce women for.' (Bukhari, etc.) From this verse and hadith, it is learned that divorce should be given in a purity without intercourse, and that divorcing during menstruation is detestable.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage explains the second type of talaq: Sunna talaq. It applies specifically to a wife with whom the husband has consummated the marriage (مدخول بها). The method involves giving three separate divorces, one in each purity (tuhr) without intercourse in that tuhr. The Arabic matn 'وطلاق السنة ان تطلق المدخول بها ثلاثا في ثلاثة اطهار' is the core ruling. The Urdu commentary clarifies that for a non-consummated wife, a single divorce makes her irrevocably separate immediately, so three divorces are not applicable. For a consummated wife, the sunna method is to space three divorces over three pure periods. The text notes that this method is less preferred than ahsan because it results in three divorces, requiring halala for remarriage. The passage then provides two hadith proofs: (1) from Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud) describing sunna talaq as a single pronouncement in purity, then waiting for two menstrual cycles before finalizing? Actually the hadith says three pronouncements over three pure periods, but it also describes a variant. (2) The famous hadith of Ibn Umar, who divorced his wife during menstruation, and the Prophet ordered him to take her back and then divorce her in a state of purity without intercourse. This hadith establishes the proper timing for divorce and shows that divorcing during menstruation is disliked. The passage emphasizes that the pure state without intercourse is essential.

Key Terms
طلاق السنة (talaq al-sunna): The prophetic method of divorce for a consummated wife: one pronouncement in each of three pure periods (tuhr) without intercourse.
مدخول بها (madkhul biha): A wife with whom the husband has consummated the marriage (had sexual intercourse).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only to consummated wives
C) To all wives equally
D) Only to wives who have not menstruated

Key Takeaway
Sunna talaq is the valid method for divorcing a consummated wife: three pronouncements in three pure periods, each without intercourse.

Sunnah and Bid'ah Divorce: Definition and Proofs
Defines and proves two types of divorce with textual evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the distinctions between Sunnah and Bid'ah divorce and explain why Bid'ah divorce is effective despite being sinful, citing the Hanafi proof texts.

Core Idea
Bid'ah divorce is sinful but effective; three pronouncements in one sitting trigger three divorces, though they violate the Sunnah.

This lesson from al-Sharh al-Thamiri introduces the two fundamental categories of divorce in Hanafi fiqh: that which follows the prophetic practice (Sunnah) and that which deviates from it (Bid'ah). The author not only defines each but also presents a robust set of hadith and athar to prove that a Bid'ah divorce, while forbidden, is legally effective. Understanding this distinction is critical for anyone issuing or receiving a divorce, as the consequences—both legal and religious—differ significantly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the definitions of Talaq al-Sunnah and Talaq al-Bid'ah. Note the key conditions: one pronouncement in a tuhr without intercourse vs. multiple pronouncements or one pronouncement in a menstruating state.
Sunnah divorce is the ideal method; Bid'ah is prohibited but counts.
2
Understand the Sunnah process
The Sunnah method requires three separate tuhrs with one divorce in each, followed by an 'iddah of one menstrual cycle. This minimizes the finality of divorce and allows for revocation.
The Prophet ﷺ instructed Ibn Umar to follow this sequence.
3
Analyze the Bid'ah forms and ruling
Bid'ah divorce occurs in two ways: three divorces in one sentence, or three divorces within a single tuhr. The text states it is sinful (makruh tahrimi) but effective, making the woman bain.
The sin is in the violation of the prophetic method, not in the legal effect.
4
Evaluate the proof texts
The author cites multiple ahadith: the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud describing Sunnah divorce, the hadith of Ibn Umar showing the Prophet's reaction to triple divorce (anger but no nullification), the hadith of 'Uwaymir al-'Ajlani applying triple divorce in a real case, and the athar of Ibn Abbas confirming effectiveness.
Key evidence: The Prophet ﷺ was angry at triple divorce but did not nullify it.

كتاب الطلاق
بها ثلاثا في ثلاثة اطهار (۱۸۸۸) (۴) وطلاق البدعة ان يطلقها ثلثا بكلمة واحدة او ثلثا جس عورت سے صحبت نہیں کی ہے اس کو ایک طلاق بھی دے گا تو وہ فورا بائنہ ہوکر جدا ہو جائے گی۔ اور دوسری اور تیسری طلاق دینے کا محل باقی نہیں رہتی۔ اور اس پر عدت نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے جس عورت سے صحبت نہ کی ہو اس کو تین مجلس میں تین طلاق نہیں دے سکتا۔ تین مجلس میں تین طلاقیں تو صحبت شدہ عورت کو دے سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کے لئے سنت یہ ہے کہ تین طہروں میں تین طلاقیں دے۔ یہ سنت طریقہ ہے لیکن چونکہ عورت کو تین طہروں میں تین طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی اور حلالہ کرانے کی ضرورت پڑے گی اس لئے یہ پہلی والی سے کم درجہ ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد اللـه انـه قـال طلاق السنة تطليقة وهي طاهر في غير جماع فاذا حاضت وظهرت طلقها اخرى فاذا حاضت وطهرت طلقها اخرى ثم تعتد بعد ذلك بحيضة (الف) (نسائی شریف، باب طلاق النبی ص ۴۷۵ نمبر ۳۴۲۳ ردار قطنی، کتاب الطلاق ج رابع ص نمبر ۳۸۴۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہر طہر میں ایک طلاق دے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ عبد اللہ بن عمر نے اپنی بیوی کو حیض کی حالت میں طلاق دی تو آپ نے رجعت کرنے کا حکم دیا پھر فرمایا کہ جب طہر آجائے تو اس میں چاہے تو طلاق دے اور چاہے تو بیوی رکھ لے۔ حدیث یہ ہے عن عبد الله بن عمر انه طلق امرأته وهي حائض على عهد رسول الله فسأل عمر بن الخطاب رسول الله الا الله عن ذلك فقال رسول الله له مره فليراجعها ثم ليمسكها حتى تطهـر ثـم تـحـيـض ثم تطهر ثم ان شاء امسك بعد وان شاء طلق قبل ان يمس فتلك العدة التي امر الله ان يطلق لها النساء (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب وقول الله تعالی یا لکھا النبی از اطلقتم النساء فطلقوهن لعد تھن واحسوا العدة ( آيت اسورۃ الطلاق ۶۵ ، ص ۷۹۱ نمبر (۵۲۵) مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم طلاق الحائض بغیر رضا حاص ۴۷۶ نمبر ۱ ۱۴۷ ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی طلاق النبی ص ۳۰۳ نمبر ۲۱۷۹) اس آیت اور حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایسے طہر میں طلاق دے جس میں جماع نہ کیا ہو۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ حیض کی حالت میں طلاق دینا مبغوض ہے۔ [۱۸۸۸] (۴) اور طلاق بدعت یہ ہے کہ عورت کو تین طلاق دے ایک کلمے سے یا تین طلاق دے ایک طہر میں ۔ پس جب یہ کرے تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور عورت بائنہ ہو جائے گی ۔ اور وہ گنہگار ہوگا۔
بدعت طلاق کی کئی صورتیں ہیں۔ ان میں سے ایک یہ ہے کہ ایک جملے سے تین طلاق دیدے۔ اور دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک ہی طہر میں تین طلاقیں دیدے تاہم طلاق دیدی تو تینوں طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی۔
حاشیہ (الف) حضرت عبداللہ نے فرمایا سنت طلاق ایک طلاق ہے۔ اس حال میں کہ عورت پاک ہو جماع کی ہوئی نہ ہو۔ پس جب حیض آجائے اور پاک ہو جائے تو اس کو دوسری طلاق دے۔ پھر جب حیض آجائے اور پاک ہو تو تیسری طلاق دے۔ پھر اس کے بعد ایک حیض سے عدت گزارے (ب) حضرت عبداللہ بن عمر نے حضور کے زمانے میں اپنی بیوی کو طلاق دی اس حال میں کہ وہ حائضہ تھی۔ پس حضرت عمر نے اس کے بارے میں حضور سے پوچھا تو آپ نے فرمایا۔ اس کو حکم دو کہ اس سے رجعت کرلے۔ پھر اس کو روک لے یہاں تک کہ وہ پاک ہو جائے پھر حیض آئے پھر پاک ہو جائے ۔ پھر چاہے تو اس کے بعد روک لے اور چاہے تو طلاق دیدے جماع سے پہلے۔ یہ اس کی عدت گزارنے کا وقت ہے جس کا اللہ نے حکم دیا ہے کہ اس کے لئے عورتوں کو طلاق دو۔

كتاب الطلاق
في طهر واحد فاذا فعل ذلك وقع الطلاق وبانت امرأته منه وكان عاصيا
(1) حدیث میں ہے۔ سمعت محمود بن لبيد قال اخبر رسول الله عن رجل طلق امرأته ثلاث تطليقات جميعا فقام غضبانا ثم قال ايلعب بكتاب الله وانا بين اظهركم (الف) ( نسائی شریف، الثلاث المجموعة وما فيه من التغليظ ص ۲۷۵ نمبر ۱۳۲۳۰ دار قطنی ، کتاب الطلاق ج رابع ص ۴ نمبر ۳۹۰۰) اس حدیث میں بیک وقت تین طلاق دینے سے آپ غصہ ہوئے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ
طلاق بدعت ہے۔
اور تینوں طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی اس کی دلیل لمبی حدیث کا یہ کڑا ہے۔ ان سهل بن سعد الساعدي اخبره ان عويمر العجلاني جاء إلى عاصم ....... قال عويمر كذبت عليها يا رسول الله ان امسكتها فطلقها ثلاثا قبل ان يأمره رسول الله اله (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب من جوز الطلاق الثلاث ص ۷۹۱ نمبر ۵۲۵۹ مسلم شریف ، کتاب اللعان ص ۲۸۸ نمبر ۱۳۹۲ ) اس حدیث میں حضرت عویمر نے بیک وقت تین طلاقیں دی اور واقع بھی ہوگئیں (۲) عن مجاهد قال كنت عند ابن عباس فجاءه رجل فقال انه طلق امرأته ثلاثا قال فسكت حتى ظننت انه رادها إليه ثم قال ينطلق احدكم فيركب الحموقة ثم يقول يا ابن عباس! يا ابن عباس وان الله قال ومن يتق الله يجعل له مخرجا آیت ۲ سورة الطلاق (۶۵) وانك لم تتق الله فلا اجد لک مخرجا عصیت ربک و بانت منک امرأتک (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب سخ المراجعة بعد التعليقات الثلاث ص ۳۰۴ نمبر ۲۱۹۷ / مصنف ابن ابی هیت امن كره ان يطلق الرجل امرأته ثلاثافی مقعد واحد واجاز ذلک علیه ج رابع ص ۶۲ نمبر ۱۷۷۸۳) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ بیک وقت تین طلاقیں دینا مبغوض ہے۔ ایک اور اثر میں ہے۔ ســــل عمران بن حصين عن رجل طلق امرأه ثلاثا في مجلس قال الم بربه وحرمت عليه امرأته (د) (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ۱۰ من کره ان يطلق الرجل امرائه ثلاثانی مقعد واحد واجاز ذلک علیہ ج رابع ج ۱۲، نمبر ۷۷۸ ارسن للمتقی ، باب من جعل الثلاث واحدة وما ورد فی خلاف ذلک ج سابع ص ۵۵۱، نمبر ۱۴۹۷۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک مجلس میں تین طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی۔ نا ایک اثر میں ہے کہ حضور کے زمانے میں ایک مجلس کی تین طلاقیں ایک شمار کی جاتی تھیں، اثریہ ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال كان
الطلاق على عهد رسول الله وابي بكر وسنتين من خلافة عمر طلاق الثلاث واحدة فقال عمر بن الخطاب ان حاشیہ : (الف) حضور کو خبر دی گئی کہ ایک آدمی نے اپنی بیوی کو اکٹھے تین طلاقیں دی تو آپ غصے میں اٹھے۔ پھر فرمایا کہ لوگ اللہ کی کتاب سے کھیلتے ہیں اور میں ابھی تمہارے درمیان موجود ہوں (ب) حضرت عویمر نے فرمایا یارسول اللہ میں عورت پر جھوٹ بولوں اگر میں اس کو رکھ لوں ۔ پھر اس کو حضور کے حکم دینے سے پہلے تین طلاقیں دی (ج) حضرت مجاہد فرماتے ہیں کہ میں عبداللہ بن عباس کے پاس تھا کہ اس کے پاس ایک آدمی آیا اور کہا کہ میں نے تین طلاقیں دی ہیں۔ حضرت عبد اللہ بن عباس خاموش رہے۔ ہم نے گمان کیا کہ وہ عورت کو مرد کی طرف لوٹا دیں گے۔ پھر فرمایا تم لوگ حماقت کرتے ہو پھر کہتے ہواے ابن عباس ! اے ابن عباس ! حالانکہ اللہ نے فرمایا جو اللہ سے ڈرے گا اللہ اس کے راستہ نکال دیں گے۔ اور تم لوگ اللہ سے ڈرتے نہیں اس لئے کوئی راستہ نہیں پاتا۔ آپ نے رب کی نافرمانی کی اور تمہاری بیوی تم سے بائنہ ہوگئی (1) حضرت عمران بن حصیر سے ایک آدمی کے بارے میں پوچھا جس نے اپنی بیوی کو ایک مجلس میں تین طلاقیں دی تھیں ۔ فرمایا اپنے رب کی نافرمانی کی اور اس کی بیوی اس پر حرام ہو گئی۔
Book of Divorce. ... Sunnah divorce is one divorce in a state of purity without intercourse. Bid'ah divorce is divorcing her three times with one word or three times in one tuhr. If he does that, divorce occurs and she becomes bain, and he is sinful. Evidence: Hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar, etc.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage from al-Sharh al-Thamiri defines the two types of divorce in Hanafi fiqh: Sunnah divorce and Bid'ah divorce. Sunnah divorce follows the prophetic practice: one pronouncement during a tuhr (purity period) in which no intercourse occurred, then waiting for the next two tuhrs with one pronouncement each, followed by an 'iddah of one menstrual cycle. This is the preferred method. Bid'ah divorce involves either pronouncing three divorces in one sentence or in one tuhr. Although sinful, the divorces are effective and the woman becomes bain. The passage cites multiple ahadith to prove both the sinfulness and the effectiveness. Notably, the hadith of 'Uwaymir al-'Ajlani shows that the Prophet accepted triple divorce as valid, though it was done in anger. The text also mentions an athar from Ibn 'Abbas that triple divorce was counted as one in the early period, but this is not the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school. The Hanafi ruling is that three divorces in one sitting constitute a Bid'ah but are effective.

Key Terms
طلاق السنة (talaq al-sunnah): Divorce that follows the prophetic method: one pronouncement in a non-menstrual purity period without prior intercourse, then waiting two more tuhrs.
طلاق البدعة (talaq al-bid'ah): Divorce that violates the Sunnah: three pronouncements in one sentence or in one tuhr, or during menstruation. It is sinful but effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a characteristic of Talaq al-Sunnah?
A) Divorce pronounced during a tuhr (purity period).
B) No intercourse in that tuhr.
C) Three pronouncements in one tuhr.
D) One pronouncement per tuhr.

Key Takeaway
Bid'ah divorce is sinful but legally effective; three pronouncements in one sitting or one tuhr constitute three divorces, making the woman irrevocably bain, in accordance with the Hanafi school's reliance on the later practice of the Sahaba.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Ruling of Three Divorces in One Session: Effective but Sinful
Explaining the ruling and evidence for triple talaq being effective but sinful

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on triple talaq in one session, identify the evidence from hadith and athar, and explain why the divorce is valid but sinful.

Core Idea
Three divorces in one session count as three and are final, but the husband is sinful for a bid'ah act.

The issue of triple talaq (three divorces uttered in a single sitting) has been a subject of legal debate across schools. This lesson focuses on the Hanafi position, which holds that such divorces are effective and irrevocable, yet the husband commits a sin. The passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri provides a detailed discussion of the proofs, including the Prophet's anger, the practice of 'Umar, and the distinction for non-consummated wives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving three divorces in one session. The ruling: the divorces take effect, the wife becomes irrevocably separated (ba'in), and the husband is sinful (makruh tahrimi).
The ruling is based on the consensus of the imams and the practice established by Caliph 'Umar.
2
Examine the first proof: hadith of the Prophet's anger
The hadith of Mahmud ibn Labid shows the Prophet's anger at a man who gave three divorces at once. The fact that the Prophet did not declare the divorces invalid implies they are effective.
The Prophet said: 'Do they play with the Book of Allah while I am among you?' This indicates the act is a serious sin.
3
Examine further proofs from the sunnah and athar
The hadith of 'Uwaymir al-'Ajlani shows that he gave three divorces before the Prophet's order, and they were accepted. The athar from Ibn 'Abbas and 'Imran ibn Husayn also confirm that triple talaq is effective.
These narrations establish the validity of triple talaq despite it being bid'ah.
4
Address the historical report of counting triple talaq as one
Ibn 'Abbas reported that during the time of the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and early 'Umar, triple talaq counted as one. The author explains that this was abrogated by 'Umar's ruling to enforce three, which became the consensus.
The abrogation is supported by the fact that 'Umar said: 'The people have hastened... so I enforce it upon them.'
5
Distinguish the case of a non-consummated wife
For a wife not yet consummated (ghayr madkhul biha), three divorces in one session count as only one revocable divorce, because after the first divorce she becomes ba'in and the remaining divorces have no effect.
This exception is agreed upon by the Hanafi school and is supported by the athar of Abu al-Sahba'.

فلو امضيناه عليهم فامضاهم عليهم (الف) (مسلم شریف، باب طلاق الثلاث ص سے ۴۷ نمبر ۴۷۲ ارنسائی شریف، باب طلاق الثلاث المتفرقة قبل الدخول بالزوجته ص ۴۷۶ نمبر ۳۴۳۵) اس اثر میں اگر چہ ہے کہ حضور کے زمانے میں اور حضرت ابوبکر اور حضرت عمر کے شروع زمانے میں ایک مجلس کی تین طلاقوں کو ایک شمار کرتے تھے لیکن اسی حدیث کے آخر میں ہے کہ حضرت عمر کو اس کے منسوخ ہونے کا علم تھا اس لئے اس کو منسوخ کیا۔ اور ان کے ہی زمانے میں بالاتفاق اس کو تین طلاق شمار کرنے لگے۔ اثر کا آخری لفظ ہے فامضاه عليهم یعنی تین طلاقیں نافذ کر دیں (۲) دوسرے اثر سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ محبت سے پہلے عورت کو تین طلاقیں دے تو اس کو ایک شمار کرتے تھے اور وہ تو ہم بھی کہتے ہیں۔ اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ ان رجلا يقال له ابوا لصهباء كان كثير السوال لابن عباس قال اما علمت ان الرجل كان اذا طلق امرأته ثلاثا قبل ان يدخل بها جعلوها واحدة على عهد رسول الله وابى بكر وصدرا من امارة عمر قال ابن عباس بلى كان الرجل اذا طلق امرأته ثلاثا قبل ان يدخل بها جعلوها واحدة على عهد النبي الا الله وابي بكر وصدرا من امارة عمر فلما راى الناس قد تتابعوا فيها قال اجيز وهن عليهن (ب) (سن سيبقى ، باب من جعل الثلاث واحدة و ما وردنى خلاف ذلك ج سابع ص ۵۵۴، نمبر ۱۴۹۸۵ر مصنف ابن ابی هبیته ۲۰ ما قالوا از اطلق امرأته ثلا ثاقبل ان يدخل بھا نھی واحدة ج رابع ہیں، ۷ نمبر ۱۷۸۷۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ محبت سے پہلے تین طلاق دے تو اس کو ایک طلاق شمار کرتے تھے۔ لیکن لوگوں نے زیادتی کی تو ان کو بھی تین طلاقیں شمار کرنے لگے۔ یہ تو ہم بھی کہتے ہیں کہ غیر مدخول بھا کو ایک مجلس میں طلاق طلاق طلاق کہہ کر طلاق دے تو صرف پہلی طلاق واقع ہوگی اور باقی ضائع ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اب وہ طلاق کا محل باقی نہیں رہی (۳) آیت میں تین کو تین ہی مانا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو ایک کیسے مان سکتے ہیں۔ آیت یہ ہے فان طلقها فلا تحل له من بعد حتی تنکح زوجا غيره (آیت ۲۳۰ سورة البقرة ٢) اس آیت میں ہے کہ تیسری طلاق دے تو حلالہ کے بغیر بیوی حلال نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے تمام ائمہ کا اتفاق ہے کہ ایک مجلس میں تین طلاقوں کو ایک مانا صحیح نہیں ہے۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, volume 3. Book of Divorce. In a single period of purity, so when he does that, the divorce occurs and his wife becomes irrevocably separated from him, and he is sinful. (1) There is a hadith: I heard Mahmud ibn Labid say: The Messenger of Allah was informed about a man who divorced his wife three times altogether, so he stood up angrily, then said: 'Do they play with the Book of Allah while I am among you?' (Nasa'i, etc.) In this hadith, the Prophet became angry at giving three divorces at once, so it is known that this is a bid'ah divorce. And the three divorces do occur; the proof is this part of the long hadith: Sahl ibn Sa'd al-Sa'idi informed him that 'Uwaymir al-'Ajlani came to 'Asim... 'Uwaymir said: 'I would be lying upon her, O Messenger of Allah, if I kept her.' So he divorced her three times before the Messenger of Allah ordered him. (Bukhari, Muslim) In this hadith, 'Uwaymir gave three divorces at once and they took effect. (2) From Mujahid: I was with Ibn 'Abbas when a man came and said he had divorced his wife three times. He was silent until I thought he would return her to him. Then he said: 'One of you goes and commits foolishness, then says: O Ibn 'Abbas, O Ibn 'Abbas! While Allah said: 'And whoever fears Allah, He will make a way out for him' (Surah al-Talaq, verse 2). And you did not fear Allah, so I do not find any way out for you. You disobeyed your Lord, and your wife has become irrevocably separated from you.' (Abu Dawud, etc.) From this athar it is also known that divorce occurs. And it is also known that giving three divorces at once is detested. Another athar: 'Imran ibn Husayn was asked about a man who divorced his wife three times in one sitting; he said: 'He has disobeyed his Lord, and his wife is forbidden to him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, etc.) From this athar it is known that three divorces in one sitting do occur. There is also an athar that during the Prophet's time, three divorces in one sitting were counted as one. The athar: Ibn 'Abbas said: 'Divorce during the time of the Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr, and two years of the caliphate of 'Umar was counted as one three divorces. Then 'Umar ibn al-Khattab said: 'The people have hastened in a matter in which they had forbearance. So if we enforce it upon them?' So he enforced it upon them.' (Muslim, etc.) In this athar, although it says that in the Prophet's time and early period of Abu Bakr and 'Umar, they counted three divorces in one sitting as one, but at the end of the same hadith it is stated that 'Umar knew it was abrogated, so he abrogated it. And in his time they started by consensus to count it as three divorces. The last word of the athar is 'so he enforced it upon them' meaning he enforced the three divorces. (2) The second athar indicates that before intercourse, if a man gives three divorces, they used to count it as one, and we also say that. Proof in the athar: A man called Abu al-Sahba' used to question Ibn 'Abbas a lot. He said: 'Don't you know that if a man divorced his wife three times before consummation, they used to count it as one during the Prophet's time, Abu Bakr, and the beginning of 'Umar's rule?' Ibn 'Abbas said: 'Yes, if a man divorced his wife three times before consummation, they used to count it as one in the Prophet's time, Abu Bakr, and the beginning of 'Umar's rule. Then when he saw people increasing it, he said: 'I enforce all three upon them.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, etc.) In this athar, it says that before intercourse, if he gives three divorces, they used to count it as one. But when people increased it, they started counting them as three. We also say that if a man says to a non-consummated wife: 'Divorce, divorce, divorce' in one sitting, only the first divorce occurs, and the rest are wasted because the place for divorce does not remain. (3) The verse counts three as three. So how can we count it as one? The verse: 'So if he divorces her, she is not lawful for him after that until she marries another husband' (Surah al-Baqarah verse 230). In this verse, it says that after the third divorce, the wife is not lawful without halala. Therefore, all imams agree that counting three divorces in one sitting as one is not correct.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, presenting the Hanafi position on triple talaq. The author first states the ruling that giving three divorces in a single period of purity (tahr) results in the divorce taking effect and the wife becoming irrevocably separated (ba'in), and the man is sinful. He then provides multiple proofs: (1) The hadith of Mahmud ibn Labid showing the Prophet's anger at triple talaq, indicating it is bid'ah but not that it is invalid. (2) The hadith of 'Uwaymir al-'Ajlani, who divorced three times before the Prophet's order, and the divorce was considered effective. (3) The athar from Mujahid and Ibn 'Abbas, where Ibn 'Abbas declares the woman ba'in after triple talaq. (4) The athar from 'Imran ibn Husayn, stating the woman is forbidden. The author then addresses a historical report that triple talaq was counted as one during the Prophet's time, Abu Bakr, and early 'Umar. He explains that this was abrogated by 'Umar's ruling to enforce three, and this became the consensus. He also distinguishes the case of a non-consummated wife: for her, three divorces in one sitting count as only one because the remaining divorces have no place after her irrevocable separation. Finally, he cites Qur'an 2:230, which treats the third divorce as final, reinforcing that three must be three.

Key Terms
طلاق بدعی (talaq bid'ah): A divorce that contravenes the Sunnah, such as triple talaq in one sitting or divorce during menstruation.
طلاق ثلاث (talaq thalath): Three divorces, either given separately or consecutively.
امضاء (imda'): Enforcement, implementation; here, 'Umar's enforcement of three divorces.
غیر مدخول بھا (ghayr madkhul biha): A wife who has not been consummated with.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a man who gives three divorces to his wife in a single session?
A) It counts as one revocable divorce.
B) It counts as three divorces and is effective but sinful.
C) It is invalid and does not count.
D) It counts as three but only if done in separate sessions.

Key Takeaway
Three divorces in one session are effective and count as three, but the husband is sinful for committing a bid'ah divorce.

Ruling on Bid'ah Divorce: Divorce During Menstruation or After Intercourse
Explaining the ruling that divorce during menstruation or after intercourse is bid'ah and sinful

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorce during menstruation or after intercourse and identify the proofs for its sinfulness.

Core Idea
Divorce during menstruation or after intercourse is sinful but valid.

When a husband divorces his wife, the timing matters. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a sunnah divorce (in a pure state without intercourse) and a bid'ah divorce (during menstruation or after intercourse when pregnancy is unknown). This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs, so you can apply the distinction correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is pronouncing divorce in two specific contexts: during menstruation, or during a period of purity where intercourse occurred and pregnancy is unknown. The ruling is that it is bid'ah (sinful) but legally effective.
The term 'bid'ah' here means an innovation contrary to sunnah, not a nullifier.
2
Locate the first dalil
The hadith of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar: the Prophet became angry when Ibn 'Umar divorced his wife during her menstruation and ordered him to take her back. This shows disapproval but implies the divorce was valid (otherwise revocation would be meaningless).
The hadith is found in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Locate the second dalil
The athar of Ibn 'Abbas: he explicitly calls divorce during menstruation or after intercourse 'haram' (forbidden) because of uncertainty about pregnancy. This strengthens the sinfulness.
This athar is from Dar al-Qutni; the Arabic is quoted in the source.
4
Understand the legal effect
Despite the sinfulness, the divorce is effective. The husband must let the 'iddah pass or reconcile if within revocation period. The sin does not nullify the pronouncement.
Hanafi ruling: validity of talaq is not conditioned on conformity to sunnah.
5
Note the application
This ruling applies to all such divorces. The prohibition is based on causing uncertainty about 'iddah and avoiding harm. The same ruling applies whether divorce is pronounced verbally, in writing, or electronically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حیض کی حالت میں طلاق دے یا ایسے طہر میں طلاق دے جس میں جماع کر چکا ہو تو یہ بھی طلاق بدعی ہیں۔ حیض کی حالت میں طلاق دینا مبغوض ہے۔ اس کی دلیل حدیث ابن عمر گزری کہ حضرت عبداللہ بن عمر کے طلاق دینے پر آپ ناراض ہوئے اور رجعت کرنے کا حکم دیا۔ اور طہر میں جماع کیا ہو پھر طلاق دی ہو اس کے مبغوض ہونے کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن ابن عباس يقول ... اما الحرام فان يطلقها وهي حائض أو يطلقها حين يجامعها لا تدرى اشتمل الرحم على ولد ام لا (ج) (دار قطنی،
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابن عباس فرماتے ہیں کہ حضور ابو بکر اور حضرت عمر کی خلافت کے دو سال تک تین طلاقیں ایک تھیں ۔ پس حضرت عمر نے فرمایا لوگوں نے اس معاملے میں جلدی کی جس میں سہولت تھی تو کیا ان پر نافذ کر دیں؟ چنانچہ ان پر تین طلاقیں نافذ کر دی (ب) حضرت ابو صہبا حضرت ابن عباس سے بہت سوال کیا کرتے تھے۔ چنانچہ انہوں نے فرمایا کہ کیا آپ کو معلوم ہے کہ آدمی صحبت سے پہلے تین طلاقیں دے تو حضور حضرت ابو بکر اور امارت حضرت عمر کے شروع زمانے میں ان کو ایک قرار دیتے تھے۔ حضرت ابن عباس نے فرمایا ہاں ! کہ شوہر صحبت سے پہلے تین طلاقیں دے تو حضور ، حضرت ابوبکر اور امارت حضرت عمرہ کے شروع زمانے میں ایک قرار دیتے تھے۔ پس جب دیکھا کہ لوگ اس میں زیادتی کر رہے ہیں تو لوگوں پر تین طلاقیں نافذ کر دی (ج) بہر حال طلاق حرام یہ ہے کہ عورت کو حیض کی حالت میں طلاق دے۔ یا ایسی حالت میں طلاق دے کہ اس سے جماع کر چکا ہو۔ معلوم نہیں رحم میں بچہ ہے یا نہیں۔
If one gives divorce during menstruation, or gives divorce in a state of purity in which he has had intercourse, this is also bid'ah divorces. Giving divorce during menstruation is detested. Its proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar that passed: that the Prophet became angry at 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar's divorce and ordered him to take her back. And the proof for it being detested to give divorce after intercourse is this athar: From Ibn 'Abbas, he said: 'As for the forbidden (divorce), it is that he divorces her while she is menstruating, or he divorces her at a time when he has just had intercourse with her, not knowing whether the womb has conceived a child or not.' (Dar al-Qutni) Footnote (a): Ibn 'Abbas said: 'During the Prophet's time, Abu Bakr, and two years of 'Umar's caliphate, three divorces were counted as one.' So 'Umar said: 'The people have hastened in a matter in which they had forbearance, so should we enforce it upon them.' So he enforced it upon them. (b) Abu al-Sahba' used to question Ibn 'Abbas a lot. He said: 'Do you know that if a man divorced his wife three times before consummation, they used to count it as one in the Prophet's time, Abu Bakr, and the beginning of 'Umar's rule?' Ibn 'Abbas said: 'Yes, if a man divorced his wife three times before consummation, they used to count it as one in the Prophet's time, Abu Bakr, and the beginning of 'Umar's rule. Then when he saw people increasing it, he said: 'I enforce all three upon them.' (c) In any case, forbidden divorce is that a man divorces his wife in a state of menstruation, or in a state in which he has had intercourse with her, not knowing whether the womb contains a child or not.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the types of bid'ah divorce. The author states that divorce during menstruation or during a period of purity in which the husband has had intercourse (without knowing if pregnancy occurred) is bid'ah and detested. He provides two proofs: (1) The well-known hadith of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar, in which the Prophet disapproved of his divorce during menstruation and ordered him to take her back. (2) An athar from Ibn 'Abbas explicitly calling such divorce 'haram' (forbidden). The text then includes lengthy footnotes that repeat the earlier discussion on triple talaq, but the final note (ج) reaffirms the ruling that forbidden divorce includes these two cases. The Hanafi position is clear: such divorces are sinful but valid. The ruling applies whether the divorce is pronounced during menstruation itself or during a time when intercourse has occurred and pregnancy is uncertain.

Key Terms
حیض (hayd): Menstruation; a state of ritual impurity during which divorce is bid'ah.
طهر (tahr): Period of purity between menstrual cycles; divorce here is sunnah if no intercourse occurred.
جماع (jima'): Sexual intercourse; the text refers to it as a condition that makes divorce bid'ah if pregnancy is unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a man divorces his wife while she is menstruating?
A) The divorce is invalid and does not count.
B) The divorce is valid but sinful.
C) The divorce is valid and recommended.
D) The divorce is invalid and requires expiation.

Key Takeaway
Divorce during menstruation or after intercourse without knowledge of pregnancy is a sin (bid'ah) but the divorce is valid and effective.

Sunnah in Divorce: Time and Number
Defining the two dimensions of Sunnah in divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two dimensions of Sunnah in divorce and explain why divorcing during menstruation is valid but sinful.

Core Idea
Sunnah divorce requires purity without intercourse and a single divorce; violating either makes the divorce valid but sinful.

This lesson explains the Prophet's recommended method of divorce according to the Hanafi school. You will learn that divorcing in a state of purity without recent intercourse is the Sunnah, but divorce given in violation still takes effect — though the husband is blameworthy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two dimensions
Recognize that Sunnah divorce has two aspects: time (tuhr without intercourse) and number (one divorce only).
2
Understand the time condition
The husband must divorce in a state of purity (tuhr) during which he has not had intercourse. Divorcing during menstruation or after intercourse in that tuhr is bid'ah.
3
Understand the number condition
Only one divorce should be given at a time. Giving three divorces in one sitting violates the Sunnah.
4
Analyze the proof
The hadith of Ibn Umar shows that divorce during menstruation counts (is effective), even though it is bid'ah. The Prophet confirmed it counts but ordered the husband to take her back.
The proof shows that bid'ah divorce is not invalid; it is valid but sinful.
5
State the ruling
Following the Sunnah is recommended (sunnah muakkadah). Violating it makes the divorce valid but the husband sinful.
The Hanafi position is that the divorce is effective in all cases.
